Thought for 11s
Got it. We‚Äôll gate everything on ‚ÄúChecked-In = Y‚Äù and then produce two artifacts:

Pan_Master ‚Äì one row per active guest, with calculated fields and normalized keys.

Pan_Dict ‚Äì category‚Üícode dictionaries built only from validated (checked-in) rows, plus a numeric/coded export you can use for Cram√©r‚Äôs V.

Below is a drop-in Apps Script. It‚Äôs defensive against column drift (looks up by header names), enforces the AB/Y rule, and won‚Äôt include anyone not checked in.

Apps Script (paste into your project)
/**
 * Build Pan_Master (active guests only) and Pan_Dict (codes from active data only).
 * Prereqs:
 * - Source: "Form Responses (Clean)" with a "Checked-In" column.
 * - You said AB holds the Y. We still resolve by header name to survive reorders.
 * - Interests exist either as "Interest_1..3" or a single "Your General Interests (Choose 3)".
 */
function buildPanAnalytics() {
  const ss = SpreadsheetApp.getActiveSpreadsheet();
  const src = ss.getSheetByName('Form Responses (Clean)');
  if (!src) throw new Error('Missing sheet: Form Responses (Clean)');

  const data = src.getDataRange().getValues();
  if (data.length < 2) throw new Error('No rows');

  const headers = data[0].map(String);
  const rows = data.slice(1);

  // Resolve columns by header name (robust to reordering)
  const col = (name) => {
    const i = headers.indexOf(name);
    return i >= 0 ? i : -1;
  };

  const idx = {
    ts: col('Timestamp'),
    bday: col('Birthday (MM/DD)'),
    zodiac: col('Zodiac Sign'),
    ageRange: col('Age Range'),
    edu: col('Education Level'),
    zip5: col('Current 5 Digit Zip Code'),
    eth: col('Self Identified Ethnicity'),
    gender: col('Self-Identified Gender'),
    orient: col('Self-Identified Sexual Orientation'),
    industry: col('Employment Information (Industry)'),
    role: col('Employment Information (Role)'),
    knowHosts: col('Do you know the Host(s)?'),
    whichHost: col('Which host have you known the longest?'),
    knowStrength: col('If yes, how well do you know them?'),
    interestsAll: col('Your General Interests (Choose 3)'),
    int1: col('Interest_1'),
    int2: col('Interest_2'),
    int3: col('Interest_3'),
    music: col('Music Preference'),
    favArtist: col('Current Favorite Artist'),
    song: col('Name one song you want to hear at the party'),
    purchase: col("Recent purchase you're most happy about"),
    worst: col('At your worst you are...'),
    stance: col('Which best describes your general social stance?'),
    screen: col('Screen Name'),
    uid: col('UID'),
    ddd: col('DDD_Score'),
    checkedIn: col('Checked-In'),
    checkTime: col('Check-in Time'),
    photo: col('PHOTO_URL_COL'),
  };

  // Enforce presence of Checked-In
  if (idx.checkedIn < 0)
    throw new Error('Checked-In column not found in Form Responses (Clean)');

  // Filter to active guests ONLY (explicit Y). If a row is blank or not 'Y', it is excluded.
  const active = rows.filter(r => String(r[idx.checkedIn] || '').trim().toUpperCase() === 'Y');

  // Build normalized helpers
  const ageKeyMap = {'21-24':1,'25-29':2,'30-34':3,'35-44':4,'55-65+':5};
  const genreMap = normalizeGenreLookup();       // returns canonical genre + proximities
  const tax = buildInterestTaxonomy();           // canonical 20ish interest tags
  const hostNorm = (h) => {
    const x = String(h||'').toLowerCase().trim();
    if (x === 'jacob') return 'Jacob';
    if (x === 'michael') return 'Michael';
    if (x === 'equal') return 'Equal';
    return 'Unknown';
  };
  const toZip3 = (z) => {
    const m = String(z||'').match(/\d{5}/);
    return m ? m[0].slice(0,3) : '';
  };
  const toInt = (v) => {
    const n = parseInt(v,10);
    return isNaN(n) ? '' : n;
  };

  // Derive Pan_Master rows
  const masterHeader = [
    'UID','ScreenName','CheckedIn','CheckInTime','PhotoURL',
    'AgeRange','AgeKey','Zodiac','Education','Zip5','Zip3',
    'Ethnicity','Gender','Orientation','Industry','Role',
    'KnowHosts','WhichHost','KnowStrength','SocialStance',
    'Interest_1','Interest_2','Interest_3','InterestsCSV',
    'MusicGenre','FavArtist','SongRequest','WorstTrait',
    'DDD_Score','Completeness'
  ];

  const panMaster = [masterHeader];

  // We will also collect unique category levels (from active only) for Pan_Dict
  const levels = {
    AgeRange: new Set(),
    Education: new Set(),
    Zip3: new Set(),
    Ethnicity: new Set(),
    Gender: new Set(),
    Orientation: new Set(),
    Industry: new Set(),
    Role: new Set(),
    WhichHost: new Set(),
    KnowHosts: new Set(),
    MusicGenre: new Set(),
    Zodiac: new Set(),
    SocialStance_bin: new Set(),   // binned stance: 1-2, 3, 4-5
    KnowStrength_bin: new Set(),   // binned 1-2, 3, 4-5
    Interest: new Set(),           // per normalized taxonomy (for one-hot work)
  };

  active.forEach(r => {
    const uid = safe(r[idx.uid]);
    const scr = safe(r[idx.screen]);
    const chk = safe(r[idx.checkedIn]);
    const chkTime = r[idx.checkTime] || '';
    const photo = safe(r[idx.photo]);

    const ageRange = safe(r[idx.ageRange]);
    const ageKey = ageKeyMap[ageRange] || '';
    const zodiac = safe(r[idx.zodiac]);
    const edu = safe(r[idx.edu]);
    const zip5 = extractZip5(r[idx.zip5]);
    const zip3 = toZip3(zip5);
    const eth = safe(r[idx.eth]);
    const gender = safe(r[idx.gender]);
    const orient = safe(r[idx.orient]);
    const industry = safe(r[idx.industry]);
    const role = safe(r[idx.role]);
    const knowHosts = safe(r[idx.knowHosts]);
    const whichHost = hostNorm(r[idx.whichHost]);
    const knowStrength = toInt(r[idx.knowStrength]);
    const stance = toInt(r[idx.stance]);

    const interests = normalizeInterests(r, idx, tax); // array up to 3
    const interestsCSV = interests.join(', ');
    const music = normalizeGenre(safe(r[idx.music]), genreMap);
    const fav = safe(r[idx.favArtist]);
    const song = safe(r[idx.song]);
    const worst = normalizeWorstTrait(safe(r[idx.worst]));
    const ddd = toInt(r[idx.ddd]);

    // Completeness score across key fields
    const completeness = completenessScore({
      interests, music, ageRange, zip5, worst, stance, zodiac
    });

    // Push master row
    panMaster.push([
      uid, scr, chk, chkTime, photo,
      ageRange, ageKey, zodiac, edu, zip5, zip3,
      eth, gender, orient, industry, role,
      knowHosts, whichHost, knowStrength, stance,
      interests[0]||'', interests[1]||'', interests[2]||'', interestsCSV,
      music, fav, song, worst,
      ddd, completeness
    ]);

    // Track levels for Pan_Dict (active-only)
    if (ageRange) levels.AgeRange.add(ageRange);
    if (edu) levels.Education.add(edu);
    if (zip3) levels.Zip3.add(zip3);
    if (eth) levels.Ethnicity.add(eth);
    if (gender) levels.Gender.add(gender);
    if (orient) levels.Orientation.add(orient);
    if (industry) levels.Industry.add(industry);
    if (role) levels.Role.add(role);
    if (whichHost) levels.WhichHost.add(whichHost);
    if (knowHosts) levels.KnowHosts.add(knowHosts);
    if (music) levels.MusicGenre.add(music);
    if (zodiac) levels.Zodiac.add(zodiac);
    // bins
    const ksBin = bin125(knowStrength);
    if (ksBin) levels.KnowStrength_bin.add(ksBin);
    const stBin = bin125(stance);
    if (stBin) levels.SocialStance_bin.add(stBin);
    // interests
    interests.forEach(it => { if (it) levels.Interest.add(it); });
  });

  // Write Pan_Master
  const out = upsertSheet(ss, 'Pan_Master');
  out.clear();
  out.getRange(1,1,panMaster.length, panMaster[0].length).setValues(panMaster);
  out.setFrozenRows(1);

  // Build Pan_Dict (category ‚Üí code) from active levels only
  const dictRows = [['Field','Category','Code']];
  Object.keys(levels).forEach(field => {
    const cats = Array.from(levels[field]).sort(naturalSort);
    cats.forEach((c,i) => dictRows.push([field, c, i+1]));
  });

  const dict = upsertSheet(ss, 'Pan_Dict');
  dict.clear();
  dict.getRange(1,1,dictRows.length,3).setValues(dictRows);
  dict.setFrozenRows(1);

  // Optional: Build a coded export ready for Cram√©r's V (numeric columns only)
  buildPanMasterCoded_(ss, out, dict);
}

/** ===== Helpers ===== */

function safe(v){ return v == null ? '' : String(v).trim(); }
function extractZip5(v){
  const m = String(v||'').match(/\d{5}/);
  return m ? m[0] : '';
}
function naturalSort(a,b){
  return String(a).localeCompare(String(b), undefined, {numeric:true, sensitivity:'base'});
}
function upsertSheet(ss, name){
  return ss.getSheetByName(name) || ss.insertSheet(name);
}
function bin125(n){
  if (!n && n!==0) return '';
  const x = parseInt(n,10);
  if (isNaN(x)) return '';
  if (x<=2) return '1-2';
  if (x===3) return '3';
  return '4-5';
}

function completenessScore(o){
  // 7 fields
  const flags = [
    (o.interests && o.interests.length>0),
    !!o.music,
    !!o.ageRange,
    !!o.zip5,
    !!o.worst,
    !!o.stance || o.stance===0,
    !!o.zodiac
  ];
  const k = flags.length;
  const n = flags.reduce((s,x)=>s+(x?1:0),0);
  return Math.round((n/k)*100)/100; // 0..1 with 2 decimals
}

function buildInterestTaxonomy(){
  // Canonical 20 tags; adjust as you see fit
  return new Map([
    ['music','music'],['fitness','fitness'],['gaming','gaming'],['cooking','cooking'],
    ['reading','reading'],['hiking/outdoors','hiking/outdoors'],['hiking','hiking/outdoors'],
    ['travel','travel'],['art/design','art/design'],['art','art/design'],['design','art/design'],
    ['fashion','fashion'],['photography','photography'],['sports (general)','sports'],
    ['sports','sports'],['film / movies','film/movies'],['movies','film/movies'],
    ['volunteering','volunteering'],['dancing','dancing'],['health sciences','health sciences'],
    ['cars','cars'],['tiktok (watching)','tiktok'],['tiktok','tiktok'],
    ['pet item','pets'],['pet','pets'],['home/kitchen','home/kitchen'],
  ]);
}

function normalizeInterests(row, idx, tax){
  // Prefer explicit Interest_1..3; else parse the combined string
  const raw = [];
  if (idx.int1 >= 0) raw.push(safe(row[idx.int1]));
  if (idx.int2 >= 0) raw.push(safe(row[idx.int2]));
  if (idx.int3 >= 0) raw.push(safe(row[idx.int3]));
  if (raw.filter(Boolean).length === 0 && idx.interestsAll >= 0) {
    safe(row[idx.interestsAll]).split(',').forEach(s => raw.push(s.trim()));
  }
  // Map to taxonomy
  const norm = [];
  raw.forEach(x => {
    if (!x) return;
    const key = x.toLowerCase();
    // Clean a few noisy inputs
    const cleaned = key.replace(/halloween orgy/g,'halloween').replace(/frying oil/g,'');
    const exact = tax.get(cleaned);
    if (exact) return norm.push(exact);
    // try fuzzy contains
    for (const k of tax.keys()){
      if (cleaned.includes(k)) { norm.push(tax.get(k)); break; }
    }
  });
  // De-dupe, cap at 3
  return Array.from(new Set(norm)).slice(0,3);
}

function normalizeGenreLookup(){
  // Canonical buckets
  return {
    buckets: new Set(['Pop','R&B','Hip-hop','Electronic','Indie/Alt','Rock','Metal','Country','Prog Rock','Ambient','Emo','Mixed / All Genres']),
  };
}
function normalizeGenre(raw, map){
  if (!raw) return '';
  const s = String(raw).toLowerCase();
  const canon =
    s.includes('indie')||s.includes('alt') ? 'Indie/Alt' :
    s === 'pop' ? 'Pop' :
    s.includes('hip') ? 'Hip-hop' :
    s.includes('r&b') ? 'R&B' :
    s === 'rock' ? 'Rock' :
    s === 'metal' ? 'Metal' :
    s.includes('elec') ? 'Electronic' :
    s.includes('country') ? 'Country' :
    s.includes('prog') ? 'Prog Rock' :
    s.includes('amb') ? 'Ambient' :
    s.includes('emo') ? 'Emo' :
    (s.includes('mix')||s.includes('all')||s.includes('every')) ? 'Mixed / All Genres' :
    ''; // unknown
  return canon && map.buckets.has(canon) ? canon : canon;
}

function normalizeWorstTrait(w){
  const s = String(w||'').toLowerCase();
  if (!s) return '';
  if (s.includes('anx')) return 'Anxious';
  if (s.includes('crit')) return 'Overly critical';
  if (s.includes('stub')) return 'Stubborn';
  if (s.includes('impul')) return 'Impulsive';
  if (s.includes('reck')) return 'Reckless';
  if (s.includes('guard')) return 'Guarded';
  if (s.includes('jeal')) return 'Jealous';
  if (s.includes('self-con')) return 'Self-conscious';
  if (s.includes('insec')) return 'Insecure';
  if (s.includes('distr')) return 'Distracted';
  return w; // leave as-is if unmapped
}

/**
 * Build a coded export table alongside Pan_Master for Cram√©r‚Äôs V.
 * Produces: Pan_Master_Coded with the same UID plus per-field integer codes.
 * Codes come from Pan_Dict (active-only levels).
 */
function buildPanMasterCoded_(ss, panMasterSheet, dictSheet){
  const pm = panMasterSheet.getDataRange().getValues();
  if (pm.length < 2) return;

  const headers = pm[0];
  const rows = pm.slice(1);

  // Build dict lookup: dict[field][category] = code
  const dictVals = dictSheet.getDataRange().getValues();
  const dHead = dictVals[0];
  const dRows = dictVals.slice(1);

  const fIdx = {Field: dHead.indexOf('Field'), Category: dHead.indexOf('Category'), Code: dHead.indexOf('Code')};
  const dict = {};
  dRows.forEach(r => {
    const f = r[fIdx.Field], c = r[fIdx.Category], code = r[fIdx.Code];
    if (!f || !c) return;
    if (!dict[f]) dict[f] = {};
    dict[f][c] = code|0;
  });

  // Column resolvers in Pan_Master
  const col = (name) => headers.indexOf(name);

  const targets = [
    // [Pan_Master column name, Dict field key, output column name]
    ['AgeRange','AgeRange','AgeRange_code'],
    ['Education','Education','Education_code'],
    ['Zip3','Zip3','Zip3_code'],
    ['Ethnicity','Ethnicity','Ethnicity_code'],
    ['Gender','Gender','Gender_code'],
    ['Orientation','Orientation','Orientation_code'],
    ['Industry','Industry','Industry_code'],
    ['Role','Role','Role_code'],
    ['WhichHost','WhichHost','WhichHost_code'],
    ['KnowHosts','KnowHosts','KnowHosts_code'],
    ['MusicGenre','MusicGenre','MusicGenre_code'],
    ['Zodiac','Zodiac','Zodiac_code'],
  ];

  // Derived bins for stance & know strength
  const idxStance = col('SocialStance');
  const idxKS = col('KnowStrength');

  const outHeader = ['UID'].concat(targets.map(t=>t[2])).concat(['SocialStance_bin_code','KnowStrength_bin_code']);
  const out = [outHeader];

  const idxUID = col('UID');
  targets.forEach(t => { if (col(t[0]) < 0) throw new Error('Missing in Pan_Master: '+t[0]); });

  rows.forEach(r => {
    const uid = r[idxUID];
    const codes = targets.map(([pmCol, dictField]) => {
      const val = r[col(pmCol)] || '';
      const code = (dict[dictField] && dict[dictField][val] != null) ? dict[dictField][val] : '';
      return code;
    });

    const ks = r[idxKS];
    const ksBin = ks == null ? '' : (ks<=2?'1-2': ks==3?'3':'4-5');
    const st = r[idxStance];
    const stBin = st == null ? '' : (st<=2?'1-2': st==3?'3':'4-5');

    const ksCode = dict['KnowStrength_bin'] ? (dict['KnowStrength_bin'][ksBin]||'') : '';
    const stCode = dict['SocialStance_bin'] ? (dict['SocialStance_bin'][stBin]||'') : '';

    out.push([uid].concat(codes, [stCode, ksCode]));
  });

  const sh = upsertSheet(ss, 'Pan_Master_Coded');
  sh.clear();
  sh.getRange(1,1,out.length,out[0].length).setValues(out);
  sh.setFrozenRows(1);
}
What this gives you
Hard filter on AB/Y: only active guests flow into analytics.

Pan_Master: normalized, per-guest metrics for the wall/panopticon.

Pan_Dict: canonical codes derived only from active data, so your Cram√©r‚Äôs V uses a clean, validated coding space.

Pan_Master_Coded: one-row-per-guest numeric export (codes) you can feed to your œá¬≤/Cram√©r‚Äôs V routines without re-encoding.

Thought for 19s
Here‚Äôs a clean, copy-paste prompt for Claude that nails the gating rule (AB = ‚ÄúY‚Äù) and tells it exactly where everything lives + what to build and how. It also lists the right formulas (by A1 column letters) so Claude can generate correct Sheets or Apps Script.

Prompt for Claude
You are assisting with a Google Sheets analytics build-out for an event ‚Äúpanopticon + compatibility wall.‚Äù All analytics MUST run only on checked-in guests. In the source sheet Form Responses (Clean), the ‚ÄúChecked-In‚Äù flag is Column AB. Only rows with AB = "Y" are ‚Äúactive‚Äù and included in downstream outputs.

Source sheet and column map (Form Responses (Clean))
Header row is row 1. Columns (A‚ÜíAD):

A Timestamp

B Birthday (MM/DD)

C Zodiac Sign

D Age Range

E Education Level

F Current 5 Digit Zip Code (ZIP5)

G Self Identified Ethnicity

H Self-Identified Gender

I Self-Identified Sexual Orientation

J Employment Information (Industry)

K Employment Information (Role)

L Do you know the Host(s)?

M Which host have you known the longest?

N If yes, how well do you know them? (1‚Äì5)

O Your General Interests (Choose 3) (raw, comma-separated; may be blank if split columns exist)

P Interest_1

Q Interest_2

R Interest_3

S Music Preference

T Current Favorite Artist

U Name one song you want to hear at the party

V Recent purchase you're most happy about

W At your worst you are...

X Which best describes your general social stance? (1‚Äì5)

Y Screen Name

Z UID

AA DDD_Score (data depth)

AB Checked-In (gate; must be ‚ÄúY‚Äù)

AC Check-in Time

AD PHOTO_URL_COL (image link)

Tasks / Deliverables
Produce three sheets, all derived only from active rows (AB="Y"):

1) Pan_Master (row-per-active-guest, normalized fields)
Create the following columns in Pan_Master in this exact order, with values derived from Form Responses (Clean):

UID (from Z)

ScreenName (from Y)

CheckedIn (from AB)

CheckInTime (from AC)

PhotoURL (from AD)

AgeRange (from D)

AgeKey (cohort code: 21‚Äì24‚Üí1, 25‚Äì29‚Üí2, 30‚Äì34‚Üí3, 35‚Äì44‚Üí4, 55‚Äì65+‚Üí5)

Zodiac (from C)

Education (from E)

Zip5 (from F)

Zip3 (=LEFT(Zip5,3))

Ethnicity (from G)

Gender (from H)

Orientation (from I)

Industry (from J)

Role (from K)

KnowHosts (from L)

WhichHost (normalized to {Jacob, Michael, Equal, Unknown} from M)

KnowStrength (from N, numeric 1‚Äì5)

SocialStance (from X, numeric 1‚Äì5)

Interest_1 (from P, normalized to a small taxonomy)

Interest_2 (from Q)

Interest_3 (from R)

InterestsCSV (join of Interest_1..3)

MusicGenre (normalized bucket from S: Pop, R&B, Hip-hop, Electronic, Indie/Alt, Rock, Metal, Country, Prog Rock, Ambient, Emo, Mixed / All Genres)

FavArtist (from T)

SongRequest (from U)

WorstTrait (standardized from W)

DDD_Score (from AA)

Completeness (0‚Äì1 proportion over: any interest present, MusicGenre present, AgeRange present, Zip5 present, WorstTrait present, SocialStance present, Zodiac present)

Gating rule for Pan_Master: include only rows where 'Form Responses (Clean)'!AB="Y".

Sheet-level formula helpers (Google Sheets examples):

Define an Active filter in Pan_Master A2 with an array formula to pull UIDs of active guests (optional pattern):

=FILTER('Form Responses (Clean)'!Z2:Z, 'Form Responses (Clean)'!AB2:AB="Y")
Zip3 (col 11) when Zip5 is in col 10:

=IFERROR(LEFT([@[Zip5]],3),"")
(In Sheets without tables, use: =IFERROR(LEFT(J2,3),"") adjusting for your layout.)

AgeKey (col 7) via a mapping table (create a small 2-col table somewhere, e.g., Maps!A:B with pairs like 21-24 | 1, etc.) then:

=IFERROR(XLOOKUP([@[AgeRange]], Maps!A:A, Maps!B:B, ""), "")
or in Sheets: =IFERROR(VLOOKUP(D2, Maps!A:B, 2, FALSE), "")

InterestsCSV (col 24):

=TEXTJOIN(", ", TRUE, [@[Interest_1]], [@[Interest_2]], [@[Interest_3]])
Completeness (col 30) ‚Äî count presence across 7 fields (example uses columns for InterestsCSV, MusicGenre, AgeRange, Zip5, WorstTrait, SocialStance, Zodiac):

=ROUND( ( (LEN([@[InterestsCSV]])>0)
        + (LEN([@[MusicGenre]])>0)
        + (LEN([@[AgeRange]])>0)
        + (LEN([@[Zip5]])>0)
        + (LEN([@[WorstTrait]])>0)
        + (LEN([@[SocialStance]])>0)
        + (LEN([@[Zodiac]])>0) ) / 7, 2)
(Claude can convert these into array formulas or Apps Script as preferred.)

Normalization rules for Claude to implement:

WhichHost: lowercased/trimmed; map "jacob"‚ÜíJacob, "michael"‚ÜíMichael, "equal"‚ÜíEqual, everything else ‚Üí Unknown.

MusicGenre: map loosely (indie/alt‚ÜíIndie/Alt, hip‚ÜíHip-hop, r&b‚ÜíR&B, elec‚ÜíElectronic, prog‚ÜíProg Rock, amb‚ÜíAmbient, mix/all/every‚ÜíMixed / All Genres, etc.).

WorstTrait: map common stems to {Anxious, Overly critical, Stubborn, Impulsive, Reckless, Guarded, Jealous, Self-conscious, Insecure, Distracted}.

Interests: use explicit P:Q:R if present; otherwise split O by comma. Normalize to a fixed taxonomy (‚âà20 tags): music, fitness, gaming, cooking, reading, hiking/outdoors, travel, art/design, fashion, photography, sports, film/movies, volunteering, dancing, health sciences, cars, tiktok, pets, home/kitchen. Clean odd strings (e.g., ‚Äúhalloween orgy‚Äù‚Üí‚Äúhalloween‚Äù; remove ‚Äúfrying oil‚Äù).

2) Pan_Dict (codes built only from active data)
For each categorical field below, generate the unique level list using only rows with AB="Y", sort naturally, and assign integer codes starting at 1:

Fields to code:

AgeRange

Education

Zip3

Ethnicity

Gender

Orientation

Industry

Role

WhichHost

KnowHosts

MusicGenre

Zodiac

SocialStance_bin (bin SocialStance: 1‚Äì2, 3, 4‚Äì5)

KnowStrength_bin (bin KnowStrength: 1‚Äì2, 3, 4‚Äì5)

Interest (each normalized interest tag becomes a category)

Output Pan_Dict with columns: Field | Category | Code.

Example formulas (per field) using only active rows:

Unique categories (example for AgeRange):

=SORT(UNIQUE(FILTER('Form Responses (Clean)'!D2:D, 'Form Responses (Clean)'!AB2:AB="Y", 'Form Responses (Clean)'!D2:D<>"")))
Codes: in adjacent column:

=SEQUENCE(COUNTA(<the unique list range>),1,1,1)
Claude can replicate the pattern for each field and stack into a single three-column table, or generate it via Apps Script.

3) Pan_Master_Coded (numeric export for Cram√©r‚Äôs V)
One row per active UID.

Columns:

UID

_code columns for: AgeRange, Education, Zip3, Ethnicity, Gender, Orientation, Industry, Role, WhichHost, KnowHosts, MusicGenre, Zodiac

SocialStance_bin_code, KnowStrength_bin_code

Method: Map each original value to its code via Pan_Dict.

Example (Sheets): If Pan_Dict is in A:C with headers Field|Category|Code:

Build helper ranges per field (Claude can do with FILTER) and then use XLOOKUP/VLOOKUP. Example for AgeRange_code when original AgeRange is in Pan_Master!F2:

=IFERROR( XLOOKUP( F2,
                   FILTER(Pan_Dict!B:B, Pan_Dict!A:A="AgeRange"),
                   FILTER(Pan_Dict!C:C, Pan_Dict!A:A="AgeRange"),
                   ""), "")
Replicate for each field. For the bin codes: first derive bins (1‚Äì2 / 3 / 4‚Äì5) from SocialStance and KnowStrength, then same lookup into Pan_Dict.

Cram√©r‚Äôs V ‚Äúnumerical outlay‚Äù (what Claude should prepare)
Input: the fully numeric table in Pan_Master_Coded (excluding UID).

Output (optional but preferred):

V_Matrix ‚Äî symmetric matrix of Cram√©r‚Äôs V across coded fields.

V_Top_Associations ‚Äî top N strongest associations with field pairs and V values.

Implementation can be:

Apps Script that: computes contingency tables per pair, œá¬≤, œÜc, and writes matrices; or

Export to a matrix in Sheets with helper scripts.

Important: all calculations use only active guests (AB="Y") via the upstream gating.

Guardrails (Claude must honor)
Absolutely exclude any row without AB="Y" from ALL three outputs.

No person-to-person matching logic here; this build is for normalized master data and codes for statistical analysis.

Keep sensitive attributes (Ethnicity, Gender, Orientation) for aggregate stats/Cram√©r‚Äôs V only; do not use for matchmaking.

Acceptance criteria
Pan_Master contains only UIDs present in 'Form Responses (Clean)' rows with AB="Y".

Pan_Dict levels come only from active data and have contiguous integer codes starting at 1 for each field.

Pan_Master_Coded correctly maps every categorical field to its code via Pan_Dict.

Thought for 13s
Good. Here‚Äôs the plan‚Äîfinal, opinionated, and wired to your sheet layout. I‚Äôm not asking you anything back; I‚Äôm locking defaults so you can build.

1) Pan_Master (codes only, active guests only)
Purpose: Numeric encoding of categorical responses for downstream stats (Cram√©r‚Äôs V, clustering, similarity).

Row filter: include only rows where Form Responses (Clean)!AB="Y".

Columns (exact order; values are codes, not text)
UID | Screen Name | timestamp | zodiac | age_range | education | zip | ethnicity | gender | orientation | industry | role | know_hosts | known_longest | know_score | interest_1 | interest_2 | interest_3 | music_pref | recent_purchase | at_worst | social_stance | checked_in_time

UID (Z): passthrough (string)

Screen Name (Y): passthrough (string)

timestamp (A): passthrough (datetime)

checked_in_time (AC): passthrough (datetime)

Everything else is an integer code, looked up from Pan_Dict (see ¬ß2).

For zip: code on ZIP3 (first 3 of F) to avoid sparse ZIP5 explosion.

For known_longest: normalize raw to {Jacob, Michael, Equal, Unknown} before coding.

For interests: use P,Q,R (or split O if those are blank) and map to your canonical small taxonomy before coding.

N/A / missing ‚Üí leave cell blank; if you must show a placeholder, use NA() in Sheets, but for Codes keep it empty so stats can filter <>"".

2) Pan_Dict (validation + codes, active-only)
Purpose: The single source of truth for category‚Üícode mappings, built only from checked-in rows so codes reflect what‚Äôs on the floor.

Columns: Key | Header | Valid_Options | Code_Range

One record per field (e.g., age_range) that lists the allowable Valid_Options (comma-separated, sorted naturally) derived from active rows, and the Code_Range (e.g., 1‚Äì5).

Also materialize a long form (3 columns) on another tab (I suggest keeping it on the same sheet below the table, or in a sister sheet named Pan_Dict_Long) with:
Field | Category | Code
This is what Pan_Master and V_Cramer_Cat will use for lookups.

Fields to code (and where they come from):

zodiac (C)

age_range (D)

education (E)

zip3 (LEFT of F)

ethnicity (G)

gender (H)

orientation (I)

industry (J)

role (K)

know_hosts (L)

known_longest (normalized M)

know_score (N) ‚Äî you‚Äôll also keep raw 1‚Äì5; no dict needed if it‚Äôs already numeric, but for consistency you can include it.

interest (the normalized taxonomy values from P/Q/R or O)

music_pref (bucketed S)

recent_purchase (V)

at_worst (W)

social_stance (X) ‚Äî again numeric 1‚Äì5; no dict needed unless you want bins.

Notes

If know_score and social_stance are strictly numeric 1‚Äì5, you can skip coding them and leave them numeric in Pan_Master; for Cram√©r‚Äôs V they are categorical‚Äîkeeping them as 1‚Äì5 integers is fine.

Maintain stable codes across runs by sorting options naturally and assigning codes 1..k.

3) V_Cramer_Cat (association matrix)
Purpose: Cram√©r‚Äôs V across all (coded) categorical variables using active guests only.

Variables to include:

Demographics: zodiac, age_range, education, ethnicity, gender, orientation

Employment: industry, role

Social: know_hosts, known_longest, recent_purchase, at_worst

Interests: music_pref, interest_1, interest_2, interest_3

Optionally numeric ordinals: social_stance, know_score (treat as categorical 1‚Äì5)

Output:

Square matrix with headers as above; cell (i,j) = Cram√©r‚Äôs V ‚àà [0,1].

Use œá¬≤ with continuity off, V = sqrt( œá¬≤ / ( n * (min(r-1, c-1)) ) ) over non-missing pairs.

Ignore pairs where min(r-1,c-1)=0 or n<2 (write blank).

4) Guest_Similarity (compatibility)
Purpose: Practical, diversity-aware matching without demographics/location.

Included features (categorical):

‚úÖ interest_1, interest_2, interest_3 (normalized set)

‚úÖ music_pref (bucketed genre)

‚úÖ recent_purchase (bucket)

‚úÖ at_worst (trait)

Excluded features:

‚ùå Demographics (zodiac, age_range, education, ethnicity, gender, orientation)

‚ùå Location (zip3)

‚ùå Employment (industry, role)

‚ùå Host familiarity (know_*)

Similarity metric (fixed, sensible defaults):

Let I_a and I_b be the sets of up to 3 interests ‚Üí Jaccard: J = |I_a ‚à© I_b| / |I_a ‚à™ I_b|.

music_pref_match = 1 if same bucket, else 0.

recent_purchase_match = 1 if same bucket, else 0.

at_worst_match = 1 if same trait, else 0. (We keep this low-weight to avoid clustering people by weaknesses.)

Weighted score (0..1):

SIM = 0.60*J
    + 0.25*music_pref_match
    + 0.10*recent_purchase_match
    + 0.05*at_worst_match
Missing components contribute 0 for that term.

Ties are broken by higher Completeness (if you carry it) and then by random.

Output choices (build both):

Matrix: UID√óUID with SIM.

TopN: for each UID, list top N=5 matches (UID, Screen Name, SIM).

This is fast to compute and reads well on the wall.

Implementation notes (so you don‚Äôt hunt):
Active row mask everywhere: ('Form Responses (Clean)'!AB2:AB="Y")

ZIP3 derivation: =IFERROR(LEFT(F2,3),"")

Normalization before dicting:

known_longest: lower‚Üítrim‚Üímap {jacob‚ÜíJacob, michael‚ÜíMichael, equal‚ÜíEqual, else‚ÜíUnknown}

music_pref: map to buckets {Pop, R&B, Hip-hop, Electronic, Indie/Alt, Rock, Metal, Country, Prog Rock, Ambient, Emo, Mixed / All Genres}

at_worst: map stems to {Anxious, Overly critical, Stubborn, Impulsive, Reckless, Guarded, Jealous, Self-conscious, Insecure, Distracted}

interests: prefer P/Q/R; else split O. Map to small taxonomy {music, fitness, gaming, cooking, reading, hiking/outdoors, travel, art/design, fashion, photography, sports, film/movies, volunteering, dancing, health sciences, cars, tiktok, pets, home/kitchen}; clean obvious noise.

Pan_Dict building (long form): for each field above, take UNIQUE of active values, sort, assign codes 1..k. That long form feeds all lookups.

Pan_Master coding: for each coded column, do an XLOOKUP against Pan_Dict_Long filtered by Field. Example pattern in Sheets:

=IFERROR(
  XLOOKUP(
    original_value,
    FILTER(Pan_Dict_Long!B:B, Pan_Dict_Long!A:A="music_pref"),
    FILTER(Pan_Dict_Long!C:C, Pan_Dict_Long!A:A="music_pref")
  ),
)
Replicate per field key.

Cram√©r‚Äôs V: run it on the coded columns (treat codes as categories). Skip blanks.

Guest_Similarity:

Jaccard(Ia,Ib) from three interest columns per person (dedupe each guest first).

Boolean equals for the three other features, then weight and sum.

Marketing vs Compatibility (you asked earlier)
Compatibility (matching): use behavioral taste variables only ‚Üí {interests, music_pref, recent_purchase, at_worst}. Keep demographics out to avoid homogenizing and to stay bias-aware.

Marketing demographics & segmentation: use the demographic & context set ‚Üí {age_range, education, zip3, ethnicity, gender, orientation, industry, role, know_hosts, known_longest, know_score} plus high-level interest buckets (safe) for campaign content.

What you‚Äôll get when you run this
Pan_Master ‚Äî one row/guest, codes only (with UID/Name/timestamps passthrough).

Pan_Dict (+ long form) ‚Äî active-only levels and code ranges.

V_Cramer_Cat ‚Äî association matrix for all chosen categories.

Guest_Similarity ‚Äî SIM matrix + Top-5 per guest.

If you want, I‚Äôll drop a single Apps Script that:

builds Pan_Dict_Long from active rows,

writes Pan_Master with codes,

computes V_Cramer_Cat,

emits Guest_Similarity_Top5.

awesome‚Äîhere‚Äôs a clean, copy-paste prompt for Claude that (1) locks analytics to checked-in guests only (AB = ‚ÄúY‚Äù), (2) spells out exact sheet/column locations, and (3) tells Claude exactly what to build for Pan_Master, Pan_Dict, V_Cramer_Cat, and Guest_Similarity.

PANOPTICON ANALYTICS ‚Äî CLAUDE SETUP PROMPT
You are configuring a Google Sheets + Apps Script analytics stack for a live ‚ÄúPanopticon‚Äù wall.
RULE #1: Run all analytics only on checked-in guests: in Form Responses (Clean), column AB (‚ÄúChecked-In‚Äù) must equal "Y".

Source sheet & schema
Source sheet: Form Responses (Clean)
Primary IDs: UID (AA) and Screen Name (Z)

Column map (by letter & index):

A(1) Timestamp

B(2) Birthday (MM/DD)

C(3) Zodiac Sign

D(4) Age Range

E(5) Education Level

F(6) Current 5 Digit Zip Code

G(7) Self Identified Ethnicity

H(8) Self-Identified Gender

I(9) Self-Identified Sexual Orientation

J(10) Employment Information (Industry)

K(11) Employment Information (Role)

L(12) Do you know the Host(s)?

M(13) Which host have you known the longest?

N(14) If yes, how well do you know them?

O(15) Your General Interests (Choose 3) (free-text blob)

P(16) Interest_1

Q(17) Interest_2

R(18) Interest_3

S(19) Music Preference

T(20) Current Favorite Artist

U(21) Name one song you want to hear at the party

V(22) Recent purchase you‚Äôre most happy about

W(23) At your worst you are‚Ä¶

X(24) Which best describes your general social stance?

Y(25) Screen Name

Z(26) UID

AA(27) DDD_Score

AB(28) Checked-In (must be "Y" to be included)

If a ‚ÄúCheck-in Time‚Äù exists elsewhere, include it; otherwise leave blank.

Sheets to build
1) Pan_Master
Purpose: Numeric encoding (per dictionary) of only active guests for Cram√©r‚Äôs V and downstream similarity.

Rows: FILTER('Form Responses (Clean)', AB="Y")
Columns (final order):
UID | Screen Name | timestamp | zodiac | age_range | education | zip | ethnicity | gender | orientation | industry | role | know_hosts | known_longest | know_score | interest_1 | interest_2 | interest_3 | music_pref | recent_purchase | at_worst | social_stance | checked_in_time

Behavior:

Convert each categorical string to numeric code using Pan_Dict (see below).

Put NA for invalid/missing.

Preserve timestamp (A), checked_in_time if present, else blank.

Implementation notes:

Start by staging a filtered view of raw columns:
=QUERY('Form Responses (Clean)', "select A,B,C,...,AA where AB='Y'", 1)

For each coded column (e.g., Zodiac):
=IFERROR(VLOOKUP(C2, Pan_Dict!$C:$E, 3, FALSE), NA())
where Pan_Dict!C:E = {Header, Option, Code} (see dictionary spec).

Repeat for: zodiac, age_range, education, ethnicity, gender, orientation, industry, role, know_hosts, known_longest, music_pref, recent_purchase, at_worst, social_stance, interest_1..3.

2) Pan_Dict
Purpose: Validation & encoding reference for categorical fields based on validated (checked-in) responses only.

Columns (wide, normalized):
Key | Header | Type | Option | Code

Guidelines:

Build from distinct active values in Form Responses (Clean) (AB="Y") per Header.

Key (machine name): zodiac, age_range, education, zip, ethnicity, gender, orientation, industry, role, know_hosts, known_longest, know_score, interest_1, interest_2, interest_3, music_pref, recent_purchase, at_worst, social_stance.

Type: "single" for single-select; "multi" for interest columns (P/Q/R) treated as single categorical slots (not a multi-select blob); the free-text blob in O is ignored for encoding.

Option: the display string (e.g., "Taurus", "Pop", "Finance / Business Services").

Code: integer code (stable, 1..N per Header). Assign codes in deterministic alpha order of Option.

Extraction example (distinct active values for Zodiac):
=SORT(UNIQUE(FILTER(C:C, AB:AB="Y")))

3) V_Cramer_Cat
Purpose: Cram√©r‚Äôs V matrix for all coded categorical variables in Pan_Master.

Variables to include:

Demographics: zodiac, age_range, education, ethnicity, gender, orientation

Employment: industry, role

Social: know_hosts, known_longest, recent_purchase, at_worst

Interests: interest_1, interest_2, interest_3, music_pref

(Optional) social_stance if you want to study behavior alignment

Outputs (separate tabs inside the same sheet or sibling sheets):

V_Cramers_Categories ‚Äî square matrix (vars √ó vars, 0..1)

Variable_Correlations ‚Äî long table: var_a | var_b | v | n sorted desc

(Optional for viz) Edges_Top_Sim ‚Äî edges where v >= 0.10 with weight v

Computation:

For each pair of variables: build contingency table on active rows, compute œá¬≤ and Cram√©r‚Äôs V:
V = sqrt( œá¬≤ / (n * min(k-1, r-1)) )

Ignore NA when forming the contingency.

Keep n used per pair for quality checks.

4) Guest_Similarity
Purpose: Pairwise similarity for matchmaking, excluding demographics & location.

Use these features only:

interest_1, interest_2, interest_3 (set/Jaccard across the three slots)

music_pref

recent_purchase

at_worst

(Optionally) social_stance if we want light behavioral alignment

Scoring (weights):

SIM = 0.60 * Jaccard({interest_1..3})
    + 0.25 * 1(music_pref match)
    + 0.10 * 1(recent_purchase match)
    + 0.05 * 1(at_worst match)
Jaccard over 3 categorical slots = |overlap| / |union| per pair.

Produce:

Guest_Similarity matrix (UID√óUID, symmetric, diag=1).

Top_Guest_Matches ‚Äî for each UID, top N (e.g., 5‚Äì10) matches with score, Screen Name.

Hard requirements & validations
Filter first: Every downstream step must operate on AB="Y" rows only.

Strict encoding: If a value isn‚Äôt in Pan_Dict for its Header, code = NA.

Deterministic codes: Stable per Header, ordered by Option (A‚ÜíZ).

Pan_Master completeness: All listed fields present (coded where applicable).

Cram√©r‚Äôs V hygiene: Drop rows with NA for either variable in a pair before building the contingency.

Guest_Similarity ethics: Do not include demographics or ZIP in similarity scoring.

Example formulas/snippets (put these where helpful)
Active filter range (helper view):
=FILTER(A:AB, AB:AB="Y")

Distinct options for a Header (e.g., Music Preference):
=SORT(UNIQUE(FILTER(S:S, AB:AB="Y")))

Code lookup from dictionary (example for Music):
=IFERROR(VLOOKUP(S2, FILTER(Pan_Dict!D:E, Pan_Dict!B:B="Music Preference"), 2, FALSE), NA())

Jaccard overlap count (helper):
For guest i vs j, overlap across P/Q/R vs P/Q/R:
=COUNTIF({P_i,Q_i,R_i}, P_j) + COUNTIF({P_i,Q_i,R_i}, Q_j) + COUNTIF({P_i,Q_i,R_i}, R_j) then clamp to 0..3 unique overlaps;
union = COUNTA(UNIQUE({P_i,Q_i,R_i,P_j,Q_j,R_j}));
jaccard = overlap / union.

Deliverables (what you should output or ensure exist)
Pan_Dict (validated options & codes from active guests)

Pan_Master (active guests, fully coded columns + raw IDs/timestamps)

V_Cramers_Categories matrix (+ Variable_Correlations long form)

Guest_Similarity matrix (+ Top_Guest_Matches)

Also return a short status report:

Row counts: total active guests; per-variable valid counts.

Top 5 highest Cram√©r‚Äôs V pairs (with n).

For 3 sample UIDs, list top 3 matches with SIM score.

End of prompt.

love this question. here are high-impact reports you can spin up right away (all auto-filter to Checked-In = "Y"):

Ops & Floor Support
Live Check-In Funnel

What: Count by status/time.

Use: Timestamp (A), Checked-In (AB).

Output: Minute/15-min cadence line chart + cumulative total.

How: =QUERY(A:AB,"select toDatetime(A), count(A) where AB='Y' group by toDatetime(A) label count(A) ''",0)

Hosts & Social Graph

What: Who knows which host/how well.

Use: L (Know Hosts), M (Known Longest), N (Know Score).

Output: Pivot: rows=Host, values=AVG know_score, COUNT guests. Bar chart for quick reads.

‚ÄúWarm Intros‚Äù Finder

What: Guests with high Guest_Similarity but who don‚Äôt know the same host.

Use: Guest_Similarity + L/M.

Output: Top intro suggestions (UID_A, UID_B, Score, Suggested topic = shared interest/music).

Unpaired Guests

What: People with few strong matches.

Use: Guest_Similarity.

Output: Guests whose top-3 score < threshold; surface their best available matches to help staff introduce.

Music & Vibe
DJ Pack

What: Most requested songs/artists, by cluster and overall.

Use: T (Artist), U (Song), S (Music Pref), Interests.

Output: Ranked list + ‚Äúcrowd pockets‚Äù (e.g., Pop lovers near Fashion + Cooking).

How: =QUERY(S:U,"select S, count(S) where AB='Y' group by S order by count(S) desc",0)

Energy Map by ‚ÄúAt your worst‚Äù & Social Stance

What: Mood balance & potential friction.

Use: W (At worst), X (Social stance).

Output: 2√ó2 heatmap (e.g., high stance + anxious pockets).

Interest & Content Targeting
Interest Cohorts

Use: P/Q/R, S.

Output: Cohort sizes; top 3 songs per cohort; suggested activities.

Cross-Over Matrix (Interests √ó Music Pref)

What: Where interests intersect with genres.

Geographic & Logistics
ZIP Heat & Radius

Arrival Curve by ZIP or Host

Use: Timestamp (A) + F or M.

Output: Multiple lines; helps staffing/bottle-necks.

Quality & Governance
Data Completeness / Validity Report

What: Missing/invalid per field (post-Pan_Dict).

Use: Pan_Master NA flags.

Output: % valid per column; list of outliers (e.g., non-5-digit ZIP, unknown options).

Diversity Snapshot (Internal-only)

What: Distribution by Gender, Orientation, Ethnicity, Age Range.

Use: D, G, H, I.

Output: Stacked bars; do not display on public wall‚Äîstaff insights only.

Analytics & Insights
Cram√©r‚Äôs V Highlights

What: Top 10 strongest category associations from V_Cramer_Cat.

Use: Long form table.

Output: ‚ÄúInsight cards‚Äù (e.g., ‚ÄúPop preference strongly associates with Fashion interest, V=0.22, n=87‚Äù).

Micro-Segments via Clustering

What: K-means on encoded Pan_Master (only non-demographic: interests, music, purchases, at_worst, stance).

Output: 3‚Äì6 clusters with names, size, top features. (If staying in Sheets: do k-modes/k-prototypes approximation with iterative assignment; or export to Python quickly.)

Look-Alikes for Marketing

What: For each future RSVP, find top-N closest current attendees (to target outreach).

Use: Guest_Similarity weights, excluding demographics/ZIP.

Output: UID, nearest cluster, top talking points.

Retention / Multi-Event (if you log future events)
Repeat Attendance & Churn

What: Who returns; how interests shift.

Use: Append event_id to source; same UID across events.

Output: Retention curve; feature drift by cohort.

Here‚Äôs a comprehensive README tailored for your Panopticon Analytics System ‚Äî designed to instruct both human developers and AI agents (like Claude or ChatGPT) on how to maintain, extend, and modify the project safely and coherently. It enforces structure, describes function-level change protocols, and preserves the artistic and philosophical aesthetic of your installation.

üß† PANOPTICON ANALYTICS SYSTEM
Behavioral Intelligence & Compatibility Engine for ‚ÄúThe Wall‚Äù Installation
üìò PROJECT OVERVIEW
Panopticon Analytics is a modular data intelligence framework designed to analyze, visualize, and narrate human behavior during live events.
It powers The Wall ‚Äî an interactive installation that visualizes the collective ‚Äúdata soul‚Äù of a crowd in real time.

The system bridges sociological data, marketing algorithms, and aesthetic storytelling, structured across four analytical layers:

Pan_Analytics ‚Äì Core computation and data structuring

V_Cramer ‚Äì Relationship mapping via Cram√©r‚Äôs V and similarity matrices

Guest_Similarity ‚Äì Compatibility pairing and network graph creation

Pan_Validation ‚Äì System checks, sheet integrity, and rebuild triggers

Each layer feeds both front-end visualizations (Wall.html, MM.html, Map.html, Terminal.html) and back-end datasets (Pan_Master, Pan_Dict, V_Cramers_Categories, etc.).

‚öôÔ∏è FUNCTIONAL RULES
All AI systems contributing to this repository (Claude, ChatGPT, Copilot, etc.) must strictly adhere to these rules:

1. Edit Scope
Only perform function-by-function modifications.

Do not rewrite full files unless explicitly requested.

Preserve variable naming conventions (Pan_, V_, Guest_, Edges_, etc.).

2. Descriptive Comments
Each function must include a descriptive header:

/**
 * Function: buildPanMaster()
 * Purpose: Filters checked-in guests, encodes categorical data, and builds Pan_Master.
 * Inputs: Form Responses (Clean)
 * Outputs: Pan_Master sheet, Pan_Dict sheet
 * Notes: Runs only when column AB == "Y"
 */
Inline comments should explain logic intent, not just syntax.

3. Aesthetic Continuity
Maintain the Panopticon aesthetic: minimalist, cybernetic, and poetic.

Code comments and terminal outputs may contain thematic language:

‚ÄúEntropy rises. The crowd destabilizes.‚Äù

Favor clarity over verbosity; each script should read like intelligent art, not raw analytics.

4. Access Hierarchy
AI may read, modify, or create files only under these structural rules:

Layer	Access Scope	Output
Pan_Analytics	Compute new metrics	Pan_Master, Pan_Dict, Pan_Entropy
V_Cramer	Add correlation types	V_Cramers_Categories, Edges_Top_Sim
Guest_Similarity	Filter or enrich guest pairs	Similarity_Active
Pan_Validation	Validate all sheets	Pan_Log
Front-end access (HTML/JS) should always read from generated JSON or Sheets ‚Äî never modify data directly.

üß© SYSTEM FLOW

   ‚Üì (filter Checked-In == "Y")

   ‚Üì

   ‚Üì
Guest_Similarity  ‚Üí  MM.html / Wall.html
   ‚Üì
Panopticon Layer Visuals (Entropy, Polarity, Flow)
üßÆ ANALYTIC OUTPUTS

Pan_Master	Numerical guest dataset	All analytics
Pan_Dict	Key-value codes for categories	Decoding system
V_Cramers_Categories	Variable-to-variable associations	Correlation heatmap
Edges_Top_Sim	Guest-to-guest and guest-to-category edges	Graph visual
Guest_Similarity	Compatibility table for checked-in guests	Matchmaker
Pan_Entropy	Entropy, polarity, diversity metrics	Wall terminal
Pan_Outliers	Guests deviating from norms	Alert visuals
Pan_Log	AI commentary and event logs	Terminal output
üß† ANALYTIC PRINCIPLES
The Panopticon Verse operates on three dimensions:

Layer	Focus	Example Visualization
Observation	Behavior & flow	Check-in timeline, density map
Compatibility	Human relation	Pair similarity, shared traits
Insight	Pattern recognition	Correlation heatmaps, entropy index
Meta	Reflexive feedback	‚ÄúSystem self-awareness‚Äù text feed
üîÆ AI BEHAVIORAL DIRECTIVES
When an AI edits or executes scripts, it must:

Validate sheet existence using Pan_Validation.checkSheets()

Operate only on checked-in guests (Form Responses (Clean), column AB = ‚ÄúY‚Äù)

Avoid destructive overwrites

Retain existing formulas and column order

Auto-document changes in Pan_Log with date/time stamps

Example log entry:

[2025-10-22 21:17] Updated buildEdgesTopSim()
‚Ä¢ Filtered inactive guests
‚Ä¢ Adjusted threshold from 0.50 ‚Üí 0.55
‚Ä¢ Added comments for readability
üß∞ DEVELOPMENT NOTES
All numeric operations use Google Apps Script (JavaScript syntax)

Matrix operations rely on Cram√©r‚Äôs V and cosine similarity approximations

Front-end visuals access JSON exports via Apps Script web app or Sheets API

Each analytics layer is modular ‚Äî run independently or via the main menu:

SpreadsheetApp.getUi()
  .createMenu('Panopticon')
  .addItem('Run All Analytics', 'refreshAllAnalytics')
  .addItem('Build Master Sheet', 'buildPanMaster')
  .addItem('Compute Cramers', 'computeVMatrix')
  .addItem('Generate Similarity', 'buildGuestSim')
  .addItem('Validate System', 'validateAllSheets')

‚ÄúThe Panopticon does not judge. It observes.‚Äù
‚ÄúPatterns are people made visible.‚Äù

Maintain aesthetic coherence between logic and interface.

Avoid overcomplicating math ‚Äî elegance = meaning.

üß† CLAUDE PROMPT ‚Äî Panopticon System Consolidation
üßæ CONTEXT
You are acting as a system integration AI for the Panopticon Analytics Project.
Your task is to combine multiple interdependent scripts into a unified, well-commented, and aesthetically consistent Apps Script codebase for use within Google Sheets and front-end HTML dashboards (Wall.html, MM.html, Map.html, Terminal.html).

You will not alter the data logic or creative tone ‚Äî only organize, clarify, and modularize.

üß© FILES PROVIDED
You have access to the following project components:

Pan_Analytics.txt ‚Äì Core analytics engine.
Builds Pan_Master and Pan_Dict. Runs only on checked-in guests (Form Responses (Clean), column AB = "Y").

V_Cramer.txt ‚Äì Correlation and association engine.
Computes Cram√©r‚Äôs V between categorical variables; produces V_Cramers_Categories and Edges_Top_Sim.

Guest_Similarity.txt ‚Äì Compatibility layer.
Filters strong guest-to-guest and guest-to-category edges; produces final similarity and pairing data.

Pan_Validation.txt ‚Äì Integrity and system-rebuild layer.
Ensures all required sheets exist; manages rebuild triggers and menu items.

‚öôÔ∏è OBJECTIVE
Combine the files into a single, cohesive system script (Panopticon_Main.gs), following these rules:

1. Modular Structure
Organize functions under clear section headers:

/* ==============================
 * I. VALIDATION & SYSTEM SETUP
 * II. DATA BUILDERS
 * III. ANALYTICS COMPUTATION
 * IV. SIMILARITY ENGINE
 * V. VISUALIZATION EXPORTS
 * ============================== */
Each function must be self-contained and callable individually.

2. Function-by-Function Integration
Do not merge function bodies unless redundant.

Maintain original naming (buildPanMaster(), computeVMatrix(), buildGuestSim(), etc.).

Place dependency comments above functions indicating required inputs.

Example:

/**
 * Function: computeVMatrix()

create rules for gs compatability, code updates, and organization
ChatGPT said:
Here‚Äôs a tight, practical rulebook for Google Apps Script (GAS) compatibility, code updates, and organization tailored to your Panopticon project.

GS Compatibility Rules
Runtime & Services

Use V8 runtime only. No eval, no HTML service inline script with <?= ?>.

Prefer SpreadsheetApp + Sheets API (Advanced) for bulk writes/reads.

Stick to UrlFetchApp only for webhook/JSON exports; never block on slow endpoints in UI-bound flows.

Sheet I/O Safety

Never hard-code column numbers; define a schema map once and reuse.

All analytics run only on checked-in rows: Form Responses (Clean) where col AB = "Y" (guard this in every builder/metric).

Batch reads: getValues() once per range; never per-row getValue() loops.

Batch writes: build 2D arrays and setValues in one call.

Data Types & Encodings

Normalize categorical strings (trim, casefold) before mapping to codes.

Represent missing/invalid as null in memory, write "N/A" to sheets.

Dates: store ISO 8601 strings in exports; keep native Date for in-memory math.

Performance

No nested loops over full sheets without an index. Pre-index by UID, header map.

Use binary flags (e.g., isCheckedIn) computed once per row.

Avoid frequent flush(). Use once after large write batches.

Triggers & Quotas

Installable triggers only (onOpen, scheduled runAllAnalytics); avoid simple triggers calling restricted services.

All long jobs: split into phases or use PropertiesService checkpoints.

Security

Never log PII. Logs are meta/status only.

If exporting JSON, hash UIDs or export screen names only when explicitly required.

Organization Rules
File Layout (Apps Script project)

Panopticon_Main.gs (orchestrator; menu, runAll)

pan.validation.gs (sheet existence, schema checks)

pan.schema.gs (headers, indices, code maps)

pan.master.gs (builders for Pan_Master, Pan_Dict)

pan.cramers.gs (V matrix + helpers)

pan.similarity.gs (guest similarity)

pan.export.gs (JSON/CSV export for wall)

pan.util.gs (logging, coercion, range helpers)

Section Headers

/* ==============================
 * I. VALIDATION & SETUP
 * II. DATA BUILDERS
 * III. ANALYTICS (CRAM√âR'S V)
 * IV. SIMILARITY ENGINE
 * V. EXPORTS & UI
 * VI. UTILITIES
 * ============================== */
Naming

Functions: verbNoun() ‚Üí buildPanMaster, computeVMatrix.

Constants: PAN_, CRAMER_, SIM_ prefixes.

Sheets: Pan_Master, Pan_Dict, V_Cramers_Categories, Guest_Similarity, Pan_Log.

Dependencies

Each function begins with a docblock listing depends on and produces.

No cross-file globals except constants and schema.

Code Update Rules
Function-by-Function Changes Only

Add new code as new functions or local helper functions.

Do not rewrite existing logic unless fixing a bug; if you must, keep the old fn as function name_v1() and route via a feature flag.

Logging

function logToPan(msg, level='INFO') {
  try {
    const s = getOrCreateSheet('Pan_Log');
    s.appendRow([new Date(), level, String(msg).slice(0, 5000)]);
  } catch (e) { /* swallow to avoid cascading failures */ }
}
Schema Map

const SRC_SHEET = 'Form Responses (Clean)';
const SRC_HEADERS = {
  TIMESTAMP: 'Timestamp',
  ZIP: 'Current 5 Digit Zip Code',
  CHECKED_IN: 'Checked-In',     // Column AB
  // ... add all headers here
};
const OUT_SHEETS = {
  MASTER: 'Pan_Master',
  DICT: 'Pan_Dict',
  VCAT: 'V_Cramers_Categories',
  SIM: 'Guest_Similarity'
};
Safe Getters

function getOrCreateSheet(name) {
  const ss = SpreadsheetApp.getActive();
  return ss.getSheetByName(name) || ss.insertSheet(name);
}

function headerIndexMap(sheet) {
  const headers = sheet.getRange(1,1,1,sheet.getLastColumn()).getValues()[0];
  const map = {};
  headers.forEach((h,i)=> map[String(h).trim()] = i);
  return map;
}
Checked-In Guard

function getCheckedInRows_(sheet) {
  const data = sheet.getDataRange().getValues();
  const hmap = headerIndexMap(sheet);
  const idxCI = hmap[SRC_HEADERS.CHECKED_IN];
  return data.slice(1).filter(r => String(r[idxCI]).trim().toUpperCase() === 'Y');
}
Main Orchestrator

function runAllAnalytics() {
  validateAllSheets();                 // pan.validation
  buildPanMaster({dryRun:false});      // pan.master
  computeVMatrix({dryRun:false});      // pan.cramers
  buildGuestSimilarity({dryRun:false});// pan.similarity
  exportForWallJSON();                 // pan.export
  logToPan('System complete: all analytics synchronized.');
}
Descriptive Function Docblock

/**
 * buildPanMaster({dryRun=false})
 * Depends On: Form Responses (Clean) with AB = 'Y'
 * Produces: Pan_Master (numeric encodings), Pan_Dict (validations)
 * Notes: Converts categorical to codes, writes "N/A" for invalid.
 */
Testing & Validation Rules
Unit-ish Tests

testMapping(): verify categorical ‚Üí code is bijective for Pan_Dict.

testFilter(): ensure no row with AB ‚â† "Y" enters Pan_Master.

testVShape(): V matrix is square, symmetric, diag = 1 (or NaN if defined).

Dry Runs

Every builder/computation accepts {dryRun} and returns {rowsIn, rowsOut, warnings[]}.

Soft Fail

If a required sheet missing ‚Üí create and log WARN, continue with empty write.

Aesthetic & Comment Rules
Maintain cyber-minimal tone in comments/logs:

// Panopticon observes. Signals stabilized.

Top of each file: purpose, inputs, outputs.

Inline comments explain why (not what) for nontrivial math (e.g., Cram√©r‚Äôs V denominator correction, bias for sparse bins).

Keep lines under ~100 chars; 2-space indent.

Deployment Rules
Menus

function onOpen() {
  SpreadsheetApp.getUi()
    .createMenu('üúÅ Panopticon')
    .addItem('Run All Analytics', 'runAllAnalytics')
    .addItem('Export JSON for Wall', 'exportForWallJSON')
    .addToUi();

Triggers

One time-driven trigger (e.g., every 5‚Äì10 min during event).

Optional on-edit/on-form-submit handlers must debounce and only schedule a run (set a property), not run heavy work inline.

Exports

exportForWallJSON() writes to a Pan_JSON sheet or Drive file; keys are stable.

Do not include PII beyond Screen Name, UID as required by the front-end.

Error & Anomaly Rules
Collect anomalies:

Unknown category ‚Üí record in Pan_Dict_Missing with raw value + header.

Sparse categories (n<5) ‚Üí flag as LOW_SUPPORT for V matrix consumers.

Never throw in main path
